Calixarenes are a prominent class of macrocyclic compounds widely used as host molecules in supramolecular chemistry due to their tunable cavity sizes and ease of functionalization. Chemists have synthesized various calixarene derivatives where pyrrole rings are introduced either at the upper or lower rim of the calixarene scaffold. These pyrrole-functionalized calixarenes can be prepared by direct substitution, condensation, or via click chemistry approaches. The incorporation of pyrrole groups can enhance the host's ability to bind anionic, cationic, or neutral guests through hydrogen bonding, π-π interactions, or coordination to metal ions. Such derivatives have been explored for applications in molecular recognition, sensing, and catalysis. Notable examples include calix[4]arene-pyrrole hybrids, which have shown selective binding for anions like fluoride and phosphate, and have been studied for their unique photophysical and
